## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This is a nonlinear harmonic oscillator where acceleration (dv_dt) depends on position x and time t. The nonlinearity likely enters through higher-order restoring force terms in x, and time dependence may indicate external driving.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Linear restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple harmonic oscillator)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Duffing with linear+cubic: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order nonlinearity)
- Driven Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (driven nonlinear oscillator)
- Driven linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * cos(c2 * t) (driven harmonic oscillator)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (pendulum nonlinearity)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric restoring force)
- Driven with damping proxy: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * cos(c3 * t + c4) (driven damped Duffing)
- Softening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2) (nonlinear spring)
- Polynomial restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (general polynomial nonlinearity)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * cos(c1 * t) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Rational restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * x / (1 + c1 * x**2) (bounded nonlinear restoring force)
- Helmholtz oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (driven asymmetric oscillator)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) → symmetric potential wells preserving oscillation symmetry
- Even-power terms (x**2, x**4) in restoring force → asymmetric potential indicating broken spatial symmetry
- Cosine/sine of time with unknown frequency → external periodic driving force
- Product x*cos(c*t) → parametric excitation where stiffness is modulated in time
- sin(c*x) as restoring force → bounded periodic potential (pendulum-type systems)
- Cubic term x**3 with opposite sign to linear term x → Duffing-type softening or hardening spring
- Rational form x/(1+c*x**2) → restoring force that saturates at large displacements
- Multiple trigonometric terms in t with different frequencies → multi-frequency driving or resonance phenomena
- Absence of explicit velocity variable suggests damping may be negligible or acceleration depends purely on conservative forces and external drive
